         <th scope="row" style="padding:0;background:transparent;text-align:left;font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/2014_Scottish_independence_referendum" title="2014 Scottish independence referendum">Scottish independence referendum</a></th>
         <td style="padding:0;background:transparent;text-align:right;">2014</td>

         <th scope="row" style="padding:0;background:transparent;text-align:left;font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">UK EU membership referendum</a></th>
         <td style="padding:0;background:transparent;text-align:right;">2016</td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="text-align:right">
          <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
           <ul>
            <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:UK_Referendums" title="Template:UK Referendums"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-talk"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:UK_Referendums&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Template talk:UK Referendums (page does not exist)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:UK_Referendums&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
           </ul>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p><b>Referendums in the United Kingdom</b> are occasionally held at a national, regional or local level. National referendums can be permitted by an <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Parliament_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Acts of Parliament in the United Kingdom">Act of Parliament</a> and regulated through the <a href="/wiki/Political_Parties,_Elections_and_Referendums_Act_2000" title="Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000">Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000</a>, but they are by tradition extremely rare due to the principle of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_sovereignty_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliamentary sovereignty in the United Kingdom">parliamentary sovereignty</a> meaning that they cannot be constitutionally binding on either the <a href="/wiki/HM_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="HM Government">Government</a> or <a href="/wiki/Houses_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Houses of Parliament">Parliament</a>, although they usually have a persuasive political effect. </p>
      <p>Until the latter half of the twentieth century the concept of a referendum was widely seen in British politics as "unconstitutional" and an "alien device". As of 2018, only three national <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendums</a> have ever been held across the whole of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>: in <a href="/wiki/1975_United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum" title="1975 United Kingdom European Communities membership referendum">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_United_Kingdom_Alternative_Vote_referendum" title="2011 United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum">2011</a> and most recently in <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">2016</a>. </p>
      <p>Two of these referendums were held on the issue of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>'s relationship with <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">Europe</a> with the first held on the issue of continued membership of what was known at the time as the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities (EC)</a>, which was the collective term for the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community (ECSC)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community (EEC)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community (EAEC)</a>, and was also referred to by many at that time as the "Common Market". This was the <a href="/wiki/1975_United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum" title="1975 United Kingdom European Communities membership referendum">1975 European Communities membership referendum</a> which was held two and a half years after the United Kingdom became a member on 1 January 1973 and was the first national referendum ever to be held within the United Kingdom. The second took place forty-one years later by which time the various European organisations (with the exception of EAEC) had been integrated by subsequent treaty ratifications into the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union (EU)</a> when the electorate was asked to vote again on the issue of continued membership in the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">2016 European Union membership referendum</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2011_United_Kingdom_Alternative_Vote_referendum" title="2011 United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum">2011 AV referendum</a> on the proposal to use the <a href="/wiki/Alternative_vote_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative vote system">alternative vote system</a> in parliamentary elections is the only UK-wide referendum that has been held on a domestic issue. The referendum was held as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_%E2%80%93_Liberal_Democrat_Coalition_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative – Liberal Democrat Coalition Agreement">Conservative – Liberal Democrat Coalition Agreement</a> which was drawn up after the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2010 United Kingdom general election">2010 general election</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">Government of the United Kingdom</a> has also to date held eleven major referendums within the constituent countries of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> on issues of <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a>; the first such referendum was the <a href="/wiki/1973_Northern_Ireland_sovereignty_referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="1973 Northern Ireland sovereignty referendum">1973 Northern Ireland border poll</a> and, as of 2018, the most recent is the <a href="/wiki/2014_Scottish_independence_referendum" title="2014 Scottish independence referendum">2014 Scottish independence referendum</a>. </p>
      <p>There have also been numerous referendums held by local authorities on issues such as <a href="/wiki/Temperance_movement" title="Temperance movement">temperance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elected_mayors_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elected mayors in the United Kingdom">directly elected mayors</a>. </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Status_of_referendums">Status of referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Status of referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Major referendums have been rare in the UK, and have only been held on major constitutional issues. Historically referendums within the United Kingdom were opposed on the supposition that they violate the principle of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_sovereignty_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliamentary sovereignty in the United Kingdom">parliamentary sovereignty</a>. In May 1945 the then Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> suggested holding a referendum over the question of extending the life of his wartime Coalition until victory was won over Japan. However, <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Deputy Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Deputy Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a> refused, saying "I could not consent to the introduction into our national life of a device so alien to all our traditions as the referendum which has only too often been the instrument of Nazism and Fascism." In March 1975 <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> also quoted <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a> that referendums are "a device of dictators and demagogues" as <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mussolini" class="mw-redirect" title="Mussolini">Mussolini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hitler" class="mw-redirect" title="Hitler">Hitler</a> had exploited their use in the past. </p>
      <p>There are two types of referendum that have been held by the UK Government, pre-legislative (held before proposed legislation is passed) and post-legislative (held after legislation is passed). To date the previous three UK-wide referendums in <a href="/wiki/1975_United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum" title="1975 United Kingdom European Communities membership referendum">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_United_Kingdom_Alternative_Vote_referendum" title="2011 United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum">2011</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">2016</a> were all pre-legislative. Referendums are not legally binding, so legally the Government can ignore the results; for example, even if the result of a pre-legislative referendum were a majority of "No" for a proposed law, <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament</a> could pass it anyway, because parliament is sovereign. </p>
      <p>For any UK-wide referendum to be held <a href="/wiki/Legislation" title="Legislation">legislation</a> has to be passed by the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">UK Parliament</a> for each vote to take place, as there is no pre-determined format or voting franchise for any such vote. However, unlike a general election there is no legal requirement for <a href="/wiki/HM_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="HM Government">HM Government</a> not to take any official position in any such vote. For example, in <a href="/wiki/1975_United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum" title="1975 United Kingdom European Communities membership referendum">1975</a> under the then Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> the government formally recommended a "Yes" vote to staying in the <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a> and in <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">2016</a> the government formally recommended a "Remain" vote to stay in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (a decision which indirectly led to the resignation of <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> as <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a> following the decision to "Leave the European Union" by the British electorate). In the <a href="/wiki/2011_United_Kingdom_Alternative_Vote_referendum" title="2011 United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum">2011</a> referendum no official position was taken as the Conservative-Liberal Democrat coalition government was split on the issue. </p>
      <p>Legally, Parliament at any point in future could reverse legislation approved by referendum, because the concept of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_sovereignty" title="Parliamentary sovereignty">parliamentary sovereignty</a> means no Parliament can prevent a future Parliament from amending or repealing legislation. </p>
      <p>Finally, under the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">Local Government Act 1972</a>, there is a provision under which non-binding local referendums on any issue can be called by small groups of voters. This power exists only for parish councils, and not larger authorities, and is commonly known as the "Parish Poll". Six local voters may call a meeting, and if ten voters or a third of the meeting (whichever is smaller) agree, the council must carry out a referendum in 14–25 days. The referendum is merely <a href="/wiki/Advisory_referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="Advisory referendum">advisory</a>, but if there is a substantial majority and the results are well-publicised, it may be influential.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Planned_referendums">Planned referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Planned referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The Labour Government of 1997–2010 held five referendums on <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolution</a>, four of which received a yes majority. Despite the number of referendums that was held during this period no UK-wide referendum was held. One concerning the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_establishing_a_Constitution_for_Europe" title="Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe">Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe</a> was cancelled, given the French and Dutch rejections of the treaty. Another, on whether the UK should adopt the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>, was never held. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> <a href="/wiki/Manifesto" title="Manifesto">manifesto</a> for the <a href="/wiki/1997_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="1997 United Kingdom general election">1997 general election</a> stated "We are committed to a referendum on the voting system for the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Despite the research carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Jenkins_Commission_(UK)" title="Jenkins Commission (UK)">Jenkins Commission</a> in 1998 suggesting an <a href="/wiki/Alternative_Vote_Top-up" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative Vote Top-up">AV+</a> system for Westminster elections, the 2001 manifesto did not make such a promise. After the inconclusive <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2010 United Kingdom general election">2010 General Election</a> the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservatives</a> <a href="/wiki/Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition" title="Cameron–Clegg coalition">formed a coalition</a>. As part of the <a href="/wiki/Coalition_agreement" title="Coalition agreement">coalition agreement</a>, both parties formally committed to holding a referendum on <a href="/wiki/2011_United_Kingdom_Alternative_Vote_referendum" title="2011 United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum">changes to the electoral system</a>. The referendum was held on 5 May 2011 and was defeated. </p>
      <p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Wales_Act_2006" title="Government of Wales Act 2006">Government of Wales Act 2006</a> became law, there can be referendums in <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> asking the people whether the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a> should be given greater law-making powers. The <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Labour_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Labour Party">Welsh Labour Party</a> - <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a> Coalition Government in the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Assembly">Welsh Assembly</a> held such a referendum in 2011, resulting in a yes vote. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a> held a <a href="/wiki/2014_Scottish_independence_referendum" title="2014 Scottish independence referendum">referendum on Scottish independence</a> on 18 September 2014. It attracted a turnout of 84.59%, the highest for any referendum held in the UK. The majority (55.3%) voted against Scotland being an independent country. In March 2017 the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> authorised the Scottish Government to seek to hold a <a href="/wiki/Proposed_second_Scottish_independence_referendum" title="Proposed second Scottish independence referendum">proposed second Scottish independence referendum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Conservative Party announced in 2013 that they planned to hold <a href="/wiki/Proposed_referendum_on_United_Kingdom_membership_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Proposed referendum on United Kingdom membership of the European Union">a referendum</a> on whether Britain should remain in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (following a renegotiation of powers between the UK and EU), in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> However, their Liberal Democrat coalition partners took an opposing stance so it was not Coalition Government policy. The Conservatives then attempted to pass the required legislation as a Private Member's Bill (the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_(Referendum)_Bill_2013%E2%80%9314" title="European Union (Referendum) Bill 2013–14">European Union (Referendum) Bill 2013–14</a> introduced by Conservative MP <a href="/wiki/James_Wharton_(politician)" title="James Wharton (politician)">James Wharton</a>), but this was not passed by the House of Lords. Following the <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2015 United Kingdom general election">2015 United Kingdom general election</a> the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> committed the new Conservative government to holding the referendum. It took place on 23 June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The referendum resulted in an overall vote to leave the EU, as opposed to remaining an EU member, by 51.9% to 48.1%, respectively. </p>
      <p>Under the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Act_2011" title="European Union Act 2011">European Union Act 2011</a> there is also provision for the United Kingdom to hold future referendums in the event of powers being transferred from the UK to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> under any treaty changes. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_and_legislation">Organisation and legislation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Organisation and legislation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>There was no independent public body to regulate referendums within the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> until the Labour government led by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> in 2000 set out a framework for the running of all future referendums when the <a href="/wiki/Political_Parties,_Elections_and_Referendums_Act_2000" title="Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000">Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000</a> or PPERA was passed, creating and giving the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a> responsibility for running all elections and such future referendums. The act also permitted the appointment of a "chief counting officer" (CCO) to oversee all future UK-wide referendums which would be held by the chairperson of the Electoral Commission. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislation">Legislation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Legislation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Separate legislation (i.e. an <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Parliament_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Acts of Parliament in the United Kingdom">Act of Parliament</a>) by the <a href="/wiki/Houses_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Houses of Parliament">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a> is required for the holding of each UK-wide referendum which is held to set out the referendum question, its format, the franchise for each plebiscite, and how each count is to be conducted. In the following is a list of legislation which has been passed by the UK Parliament to enable the holding of the following UK-wide referendums. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Referendum_Act_1975" title="Referendum Act 1975">Referendum Act 1975</a> (United Kingdom European Communities membership referendum, 1975)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Voting_System_and_Constituencies_Act_2011" title="Parliamentary Voting System and Constituencies Act 2011">Parliamentary Voting System and Constituencies Act 2011</a> (United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum, 2011)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/European_Union_Referendum_Act_2015" title="European Union Referendum Act 2015">European Union Referendum Act 2015</a> (United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016)</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_referendums">National referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: National referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>To date only three referendums have been held which have covered the whole of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. The following is a description of each of the three national referendums. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1975_European_Communities_membership_referendum">1975 European Communities membership referendum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1975 European Communities membership referendum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: 
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum,_1975" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom European Communities membership referendum, 1975">United Kingdom European Communities membership referendum, 1975</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum,_1975.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum%2C_1975.svg/180px-United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum%2C_1975.svg.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="333" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum%2C_1975.svg/270px-United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum%2C_1975.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum%2C_1975.svg/360px-United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum%2C_1975.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="321" data-file-height="594"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_European_Communities_membership_referendum,_1975.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>All but two areas voted "Yes"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On Thursday 5 June 1975 the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> held its first ever nationwide referendum on whether to continue its membership of the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a> (EC) principally the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC, or "Common Market") as it was more widely known at the time. The UK had been a member of the EC since 1 January 1973 and the vote came about after a manifesto commitment by the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour Party UK">Labour Party</a> under the then Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> in the <a href="/wiki/October_1974_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="October 1974 United Kingdom general election">UK General Election in October 1974</a> and following a renegotiation of EC membership. All of the major political parties and mainstream press supported continuing membership of the EC. However, there were significant splits within the ruling Labour party, the membership of which had voted 2:1 in favour of withdrawal at a one-day <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour Party (UK) Conference">party conference</a> on 26 April 1975. Since the cabinet was split between strongly <a href="/wiki/Pro-Europeanism" title="Pro-Europeanism">pro-European</a> and strongly <a href="/wiki/Euroscepticism" title="Euroscepticism">anti-European</a> ministers, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> suspended the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_convention_(political_custom)" title="Constitutional convention (political custom)">constitutional convention</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_collective_responsibility" title="Cabinet collective responsibility">Cabinet collective responsibility</a> and allowed ministers to publicly campaign on either side. Seven of the twenty-three members of the cabinet opposed EC membership and the party was formally neutral on the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The referendum which was non-binding was conducted in its entirety under the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/Referendum_Act_1975" title="Referendum Act 1975">Referendum Act 1975</a> as there was no prior procedure or legislation within the United Kingdom for the holding of any such plebiscite. The two campaign groups in the referendum were "Britain in Europe" advocating a yes vote and "National Referendum Campaign" advocating a no vote. </p>
      <p>The voters were asked to vote "Yes" or "No" on the question: "Do you think the United Kingdom should stay in the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Community</a> (the Common Market)?" Of the 68 counting areas in the counties and administrative regions of the UK who voted "Yes", only the <a href="/wiki/Shetland_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Shetland Islands">Shetland Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a> voted "No". In line with the outcome of the vote, the United Kingdom remained a member of the European Communities which would later become the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:right; font-size:100%;">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_Alternative_Vote_referendum">2011 Alternative Vote referendum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2011 Alternative Vote referendum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_AV_referendum_area_results.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/United_Kingdom_AV_referendum_area_results.svg/200px-United_Kingdom_AV_referendum_area_results.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="296" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/United_Kingdom_AV_referendum_area_results.svg/300px-United_Kingdom_AV_referendum_area_results.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/United_Kingdom_AV_referendum_area_results.svg/400px-United_Kingdom_AV_referendum_area_results.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="871" data-file-height="1289"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_AV_referendum_area_results.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>All but ten areas voted "No"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: 
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Alternative_Vote_referendum,_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum, 2011">United Kingdom Alternative Vote referendum, 2011</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The alternative vote referendum, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_%E2%80%93_Liberal_Democrat_Coalition_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative – Liberal Democrat Coalition Agreement">Conservative – Liberal Democrat Coalition Agreement</a> drawn up after the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2010 United Kingdom general election">2010 general election</a>, was a nationwide vote held on Thursday 5 May 2011 (the same date as local elections in many areas) to choose the method of electing MPs at subsequent general elections. The referendum concerned whether to replace the present "<a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post</a>" system with the "<a href="/wiki/Instant-runoff_voting" title="Instant-runoff voting">alternative vote</a>" (AV) method. The voters were asked to vote yes or no on the question "At present, the UK uses the "first past the post" system to elect MPs to the House of Commons. Should the "alternative vote" system be used instead?". It was the first nationwide referendum to be held for some thirty six years and was legislated for under the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Voting_System_and_Constituencies_Act_2011" title="Parliamentary Voting System and Constituencies Act 2011">Parliamentary Voting System and Constituencies Act 2011</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Political_Parties,_Elections_and_Referendums_Act_2000" title="Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000">Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000</a> and is to date the first and only UK-wide referendum to be held on a domestic issue. Turnout was low at just 42% nationally and was also marked by relatively low key campaigning. The two campaigning groups for the referendum was advocating a yes vote <a href="/wiki/Yes_to_Fairer_Votes" class="mw-redirect" title="Yes to Fairer Votes">Yes to Fairer Votes</a> and advocating a no vote <a href="/wiki/NOtoAV" title="NOtoAV">NOtoAV</a>. </p>
      <p>AV was rejected by 67% of voters with all but ten of the 440 voting areas voted "No" and the proposed legislation to introduce AV which was subject to the referendum was repealed. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_European_Union_membership_referendum">2016 European Union membership referendum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2016 European Union membership referendum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg/200px-United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="296" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg/300px-United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg/400px-United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="871" data-file-height="1289"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A total of 263 voting areas voted to "Leave" whereas 119 voting areas voted to "Remain" in the referendum. 
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0069b5; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Leave
         </div> 
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffc010; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Remain
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: 
       <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On Thursday 23 June 2016 the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> voted for the second time in 41 years on its membership to what is now known as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) with the overseas territory <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> also voting on the issue for the very first time. The referendum was called after <a href="/wiki/Conservatives_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservatives (UK)">Conservative</a> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> made a manifesto commitment in the <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2015 United Kingdom general election">2015 United Kingdom general election</a> to undertake a renegotiation of the UK's membership to the European Union which would be followed by a in-out referendum. All of the major political parties were in favour of remaining an EU member, except for a split within the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>. The cabinet was split between pro-EU and anti-EU ministers, and Cameron suspended the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_convention_(political_custom)" title="Constitutional convention (political custom)">constitutional convention</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_collective_responsibility" title="Cabinet collective responsibility">Cabinet collective responsibility</a>, allowing ministers to publicly campaign on either side. Seven of the 23 members of the Cabinet opposed continued EU membership. </p>
      <p>The referendum was legislated for under the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Referendum_Act_2015" title="European Union Referendum Act 2015">European Union Referendum Act 2015</a>, which legally required <a href="/wiki/HM_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="HM Government">HM Government</a> to hold the referendum no later than 31 December 2017 and also the <a href="/wiki/Political_Parties,_Elections_and_Referendums_Act_2000" title="Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000">Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000</a>. Voters were asked to vote "Remain a member of the European Union" or "Leave the European Union" on the question "Should the United Kingdom remain a member of the European Union or leave the European Union?" The main campaign groups for the referendum were advocating a "remain" vote was <a href="/wiki/Britain_Stronger_in_Europe" title="Britain Stronger in Europe">Britain Stronger in Europe</a> and advocating a "leave" vote was <a href="/wiki/Vote_Leave" title="Vote Leave">Vote Leave</a>. </p>
      <p>The "Leave" option was voted by 52% of voters, as opposed to 48% of voters who wished to "Remain". Of the 382 voting areas, 263 returned majority votes in favour of "Leave" whereas 119 returned majority votes in favour of "Remain" which included every <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Scotland" title="Local government in Scotland">Scottish council area</a> and all but five of the <a href="/wiki/London_borough" class="mw-redirect" title="London borough">London boroughs</a>. The vote revealed divisions among the constituent nations of the United Kingdom, with <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> voting to leave, but <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> voting to remain. The national turnout was 72% which was eight percentage points higher than the turnout back in 1975, although the majority was 12 percentage points lower. It was the first time a UK-wide referendum result had gone against the preferred choice of <a href="/wiki/HM_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="HM Government">HM Government</a> who had officially recommended a "Remain" vote and it led to a period of political turmoil. As a direct consequence of losing the referendum, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> announced his resignation as Prime Minister on the morning after the vote. He left office three weeks later on 13 July, and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> who later resigned in 2019 due to the issue remaining unresolved. After the vote there was frequent public discussion whether the result of the referendum was advisory or mandatory, but the High Court stated on 3 November 2016 that, in the absence of specific provision in the enabling legislation (such as in this case there was not), 'a referendum on any topic can only be advisory for the lawmakers in Parliament”<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>. </p>
      <p><br> </p>

      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_other_major_referendums">List of other major referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: List of other major referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Since 1973 there have been eleven other referendums held by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">Government of the United Kingdom</a> within the constituent countries related to the issues of sovereignty, devolution and independence in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> and in parts of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> (in the <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East</a> and <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="England">England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/1998_Greater_London_Authority_referendum" title="1998 Greater London Authority referendum">1998 Greater London Authority referendum</a>, on whether there should be a <a href="/wiki/Greater_London_Authority" title="Greater London Authority">Greater London Authority</a>, consisting of a <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_London" title="Mayor of London">Mayor of London</a> and a <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a> (yes)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/2004_North_East_England_devolution_referendum" title="2004 North East England devolution referendum">2004 North East England devolution referendum</a>, on an elected regional assembly (no)</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Ireland">Northern Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Northern Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/1973_Northern_Ireland_sovereignty_referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="1973 Northern Ireland sovereignty referendum">1973 Northern Ireland sovereignty referendum</a>, on whether <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> should leave the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (UK) and join the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> (no)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/1998_Northern_Ireland_Belfast_Agreement_referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="1998 Northern Ireland Belfast Agreement referendum">1998 Northern Ireland Belfast Agreement referendum</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> (yes)</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scotland">Scotland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Scotland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/1979_Scottish_devolution_referendum" title="1979 Scottish devolution referendum">1979 Scottish devolution referendum</a>, on whether there should be a <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Assembly" title="Scottish Assembly">Scottish Assembly</a> (small majority voted yes, but fell short of the <a href="/wiki/1979_Scottish_devolution_referendum#Results" title="1979 Scottish devolution referendum">40% threshold</a> required to enact devolution)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/1997_Scottish_devolution_referendum" title="1997 Scottish devolution referendum">1997 Scottish devolution referendum</a>, Two questions: On whether there should be a <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> (yes); On whether a Scottish Parliament should have tax varying powers (yes)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/2014_Scottish_independence_referendum" title="2014 Scottish independence referendum">2014 Scottish independence referendum</a> on the question "Should Scotland be an independent country?", 18 September 2014 (no)</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wales">Wales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Wales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/1979_Welsh_devolution_referendum" title="1979 Welsh devolution referendum">1979 Welsh devolution referendum</a>, on whether there should be a <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">Welsh Assembly</a> (no)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/1997_Welsh_devolution_referendum" title="1997 Welsh devolution referendum">1997 Welsh devolution referendum</a>, on whether there should be a <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a> (yes)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/2011_Welsh_devolution_referendum" title="2011 Welsh devolution referendum">2011 Welsh devolution referendum</a>, on whether the National Assembly should have increased law-making powers (yes)</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_referendums">Local referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Local referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Referendums have been held in local areas in England, Wales and Scotland since 1913. These have covered issues such as local government administration, transport, <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_of_alcohol" class="mw-redirect" title="Prohibition of alcohol">prohibition</a>, and other local questions. The areas covered have generally corresponded to local authority areas, civil parishes, or <a href="/wiki/Wards_and_electoral_divisions_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Wards and electoral divisions of the United Kingdom">wards</a>, with all local government electors of the relevant area being eligible to vote. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advisory_referendums">Advisory referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Advisory referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Principal authorities in Great Britain have the ability to hold an advisory referendum on any issue relating to its services, financial provisions, and other matters that are relevant to the area.<sup id="cite_ref-LRBriefing_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRBriefing-10">[10]</a></sup> The power for principal local authorities to hold a poll within England and Wales is specifically granted by the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_2003" title="Local Government Act 2003">Local Government Act 2003</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> previously local polls relied upon a council's power to consult residents and collect information.<sup id="cite_ref-LRBriefing_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRBriefing-10">[10]</a></sup> In Scotland the power is similarly implied by the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_(Scotland)_Act_1973" title="Local Government (Scotland) Act 1973">Local Government (Scotland) Act 1973</a>, and an additional power is conferred by the requirement of the Transport (Scotland) Act 2001 to consult before introducing a road charging scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-LRBriefing_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRBriefing-10">[10]</a></sup> The power to hold local referendums has not been extended to Northern Ireland. </p>
      <p>A local advisory referendum is not required to follow the legislation governing the conduct of other referendums and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Elections in the United Kingdom">elections in the UK</a>. The local authority can choose how to conduct a local referendum, and may choose to hold the <a href="/wiki/Postal_voting" title="Postal voting">vote solely by post</a>, instead of using <a href="/wiki/Polling_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Polling station">polling stations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_referendums">Transport referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transport referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: 
       <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_road_tolls_referendum,_2005" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh road tolls referendum, 2005">Edinburgh road tolls referendum, 2005</a> and 
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_transport_referendum,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Manchester transport referendum, 2008">Greater Manchester transport referendum, 2008</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/City_of_Edinburgh_Council" title="City of Edinburgh Council">City of Edinburgh Council</a> held a postal-ballot referendum in February 2005 over whether voters supported the Council's proposed transport strategy. These plans included a <a href="/wiki/Congestion_charge" class="mw-redirect" title="Congestion charge">congestion charge</a> which would have required motorists to pay a fee to enter the city at certain times of the day. The result was announced on 22 February 2005 and the people of Edinburgh had rejected the proposals. 74% voted against, 26% voted in favour, and the turnout was 62%. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Strathclyde_water_referendum">Strathclyde water referendum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Strathclyde water referendum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/Strathclyde_water_referendum,_1994" class="mw-redirect" title="Strathclyde water referendum, 1994">Strathclyde water referendum, 1994</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Strathclyde_Regional_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Strathclyde Regional Council">Strathclyde Regional Council</a> held a referendum in 1994 on the plans of the Conservative UK government to privatise water services within Scotland. The government planned to sell the three recently established water authorities in Scotland, created under the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_etc._(Scotland)_Act_1994" title="Local Government etc. (Scotland) Act 1994">Local Government etc. (Scotland) Act 1994</a> as a precursor for privatisation, which would bring Scotland in line with <a href="/wiki/Water_privatisation_in_England_and_Wales" title="Water privatisation in England and Wales">the 1989 privatisation in England and Wales</a>. Strathclyde council, which previously held responsibility for water services, planned the referendum in response to overwhelming public opinion against the move. The referendum, conducted <a href="/wiki/Postal_voting" title="Postal voting">by post</a>, resulted in 97% voting against the plan, with 70% of the electorate participating. Although the referendum had no legal effect, the plan to privatise Scottish water services was eventually dropped. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statutory_referendums">Statutory referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Statutory referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Legislation in England and Wales obliges local authorities to hold and abide by the results of referendums in certain circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-LRBriefing_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRBriefing-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In England, raising <a href="/wiki/Council_Tax" title="Council Tax">Council Tax</a> above a level proscribed by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Communities_and_Local_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for Communities and Local Government">Local Government Secretary</a> requires approval in a referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-CTaxB_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CTaxB-13">[13]</a></sup> The threshold was initially set at 2% in 2012 for all types of local authority, but for authorities that fund social care the threshold was increased to 4% in 2015 and 5% in 2017. From April 2018 the figures for both types of authority have been increased by an additional 1%.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> This provision applies to all <a href="/wiki/Council_Tax#Precepting_authorities" title="Council Tax">precepting authorities</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[note 1]</a></sup> when this is not the billing authority (i.e. the district council), the latter will hold the referendum on the precepting authority's behalf, and recoup the costs. Only one council tax referendum has been held, on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Bedfordshire_Police_and_Crime_Commissioner" title="Bedfordshire Police and Crime Commissioner">Bedfordshire Police and Crime Commissioner</a>, and the rise was rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> A proposal for a referendum to increase the council tax for <a href="/wiki/Surrey_County_Council" title="Surrey County Council">Surrey County Council</a> by 15% was initially approved by the council, but plans for the increase were abandoned before the referendum could go ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Localism_Act_2011" title="Localism Act 2011">Localism Act 2011</a> allows parish councils or local community groups to create neighbourhood development plans. The plans are intended to guide <a href="/wiki/Town_and_country_planning_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Town and country planning in the United Kingdom">planning decisions</a> within the neighbourhood area, by outlining the amount and type of development that should occur in the area, what land may be built upon and how existing buildings may be reused. For a plan to come into force, it must be approved by the electorate in the local area in a referendum. Neighbourhood planning referendums have a high success rate, with all being approved as of December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-LRBriefing_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRBriefing-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayoral_and_other_governance_referendums">Mayoral and other governance referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mayoral and other governance referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales_mayoral_referendums" title="England and Wales mayoral referendums">England and Wales mayoral referendums</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A local authority in England and Wales can hold a referendum on changing its <a href="/wiki/Executive_arrangements" title="Executive arrangements">executive arrangements</a> between a directly elected mayor, a leader and cabinet, and in England only, a committee system.<sup id="cite_ref-LRBriefing_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRBriefing-10">[10]</a></sup> A referendum can be held by three methods; by a resolution of the council to hold one, under an order from the government, or upon receiving a petition signed by five percent of registered voters within the local authority area,<sup id="cite_ref-RefMayor_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefMayor-18">[17]</a></sup> in the only example of the <a href="/wiki/Initiative" title="Initiative">initiative</a> process in the United Kingdom. If successful, the council must change its governance system, and hold an election for the mayor if necessary. </p>
      <p>The process differs between England and Wales. In England, a referendum can be held on moving between any of the three systems, and following the vote another referendum may not be held for 10 years. A council is not required to hold a referendum to change its executive arrangements,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[note 2]</a></sup> but a change that has occurred as a result of a referendum can only be changed following another referendum. In Wales, a council must hold a referendum to change between a mayor and leader and cabinet, with the minimum period between votes set at five years.<sup id="cite_ref-RefMayor_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefMayor-18">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Fifty-three referendums have taken place in local authorities to establish whether there is support for <a href="/wiki/Elected_mayors_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elected mayors in the United Kingdom">directly elected mayors</a>. Sixteen were successful and a mayoralty was established; in thirty-seven local authorities an elected mayor was rejected by voters. An additional six referendums have been held on removing the post of elected mayor, with three mayoralties being retained, and three disestablished.<sup id="cite_ref-RefMayor_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefMayor-18">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2012_English_mayoral_referendums" title="2012 English mayoral referendums">Ten referendums were held in 2012</a> as part of the government's <a href="/wiki/Manifesto" title="Manifesto">manifesto</a> to introduce elected mayors in the largest cities in England without the position.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> Only one new mayoralty was approved, and no further votes have been ordered by the government. Two referendums have been held in response to a petition on moving to a committee system, in the <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Fylde" title="Borough of Fylde">Borough of Fylde</a> and in <a href="/wiki/West_Dorset" title="West Dorset">West Dorset</a>. Both referendums were successful.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> On average, turnout is similar to that of local elections, with the highest turnout 64% in <a href="/wiki/Berwick-upon-Tweed" title="Berwick-upon-Tweed">Berwick-upon-Tweed</a> (held alongside the <a href="/wiki/2001_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2001 United Kingdom general election">2001 general election</a>) and the lowest 10% in the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Ealing" title="London Borough of Ealing">London Borough of Ealing</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Prohibition_referendums">Prohibition referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Prohibition referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Temperance_movement" title="Temperance movement">temperance movement</a> led to two countries of the UK gaining the right to hold referendums on the sale of alcohol in the local area, upon the request of a number of local electors. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Temperance_(Scotland)_Act_1913" title="Temperance (Scotland) Act 1913">Temperance (Scotland) Act 1913</a> provided that polls could be held in small local areas in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> to determine whether to instate a level of <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_of_alcohol" class="mw-redirect" title="Prohibition of alcohol">prohibition</a> on the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverages" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverages">alcoholic beverages</a>; the provisions were later incorporated into the Licensing (Scotland) Act 1959. Between 1913 and 1965 1,131 such polls were held, with the vast majority (1,079) held before 1930.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> These provisions and the local polls were abolished by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Licensing_(Scotland)_Act_1976&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Licensing (Scotland) Act 1976 (page does not exist)">Licensing (Scotland) Act 1976</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Closing_(Wales)_Act_1881" title="Sunday Closing (Wales) Act 1881">Sunday Closing (Wales) Act 1881</a> mandated that all <a href="/wiki/Public_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Public house">public houses</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> be closed on Sundays. The Act was extended to <a href="/wiki/Monmouthshire_(historic)" title="Monmouthshire (historic)">Monmouthshire</a> in 1921. Under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Licensing_Act_1961" class="mw-redirect" title="Licensing Act 1961">Licensing Act 1961</a>, on the application of 500 local electors, a referendum could be held in each local government area at seven-year intervals on whether that district should be "wet" or "dry" on the Sabbath. Most districts in the border area and the southern industrial area went "wet" in 1961 or 1968, with most others following suit in 1975. In 1982, the last district, <a href="/wiki/Dwyfor" title="Dwyfor">Dwyfor</a>, in western Gwynedd, went "wet" and it was thought that the influence of the Sabbatarian temperance movement had expired and few referendums were called, but surprisingly a further referendum was called in Dwyfor in 1989 and the area went "dry" for another seven years on a 9% turnout. The whole of Wales was "wet" from 1996, and the facility for further referendums was removed by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sunday_Licensing_Act_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sunday Licensing Act 2003 (page does not exist)">Sunday Licensing Act 2003</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parish_polls">Parish polls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Parish polls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>A parish poll is a referendum held in a civic parish under the Local Government Act 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> The cost of holding such polls is met by the parish council.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>"A poll may be demanded before the conclusion of a community meeting on any question arising at the meeting; but no poll shall be taken unless either the person presiding at the meeting consents or the poll is demanded by not less than ten, or one-third, of the local government electors present at the meeting, whichever is the less."<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2007, villagers in <a href="/wiki/East_Stoke,_Dorset" title="East Stoke, Dorset">East Stoke</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a> forced a referendum, under the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">Local Government Act 1972</a>, on this question: "Do You Want a Referendum on the EU Constitutional Treaty? Yes or No?" Of the 339 people who were eligible to vote, 80 voted: 72 votes for Yes and 8 votes for No. The poll was initiated by a supporter of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Independence_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Independence Party">United Kingdom Independence Party</a>, a political party noted for its <a href="/wiki/Euroscepticism" title="Euroscepticism">Euroscepticism</a>. The poll was criticised by the chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Parish_councils_in_England" title="Parish councils in England">parish council</a> as "little more than a publicity stunt."<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

       <li><a href="/wiki/Category:Referendums_in_British_Overseas_Territories" title="Category:Referendums in British Overseas Territories">Category:Referendums in British Overseas Territories</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Referendums_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although the legislation includes <a href="/wiki/Parish_councils_in_England" title="Parish councils in England">parish councils</a>, the government does not currently enforce a cap.<sup id="cite_ref-CTaxB_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CTaxB-13">[13]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A council can adopt a Mayor with a resolution approved by two-thirds of the councillors.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
